  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_730252e8-f591-4a10-9de6-e49a61fa0237'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

  <span id="freeText2980240281999106865" style="display:none"><i>If you could make one simple choice that would change your life forever, would you?</i><br /><br />Erin is a documentary filmmaker on the brink of a professional breakthrough, Mark a handsome investment banker with big plans. Passionately in love, they embark on a dream honeymoon to the tropical island of Bora Bora, where they enjoy the sun, the sand, and each other. Then, while scuba diving in the crystal blue sea, they find something in the water. . . .<br /><br /><i>Could the life of your dreams be the stuff of nightmares?</i><br /><br />Suddenly the newlyweds must make a dangerous choice: to speak out or to protect their secret. After all, if no one else knows, who would be hurt? Their decision will trigger a devastating chain of events. . . .<br /><br /><i>Have you ever wondered how long it takes to dig a grave?</i><br /><br />Wonder no longer. Catherine Steadman's enthralling voice shines throughout this spellbinding debut novel. With piercing insight and fascinating twists, <i>Something in the Water</i> challenges the reader to confront the hopes we desperately cling to, the ideals we're tempted to abandon, and the perfect lies we tell ourselves.</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    I totally agree with these comments. I loved the suspense in the middle, rolled my eyes so much (I don't think I've ever been so frustrated with a pro<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    I totally agree with these comments. I loved the suspense in the middle, rolled my eyes so much (I don't think I've ever been so frustrated with a protagonist), but the ending left me with so many questions. 1) What was Eddie's last favor??, 2) What WAS Patrick's role? I figured it was Mark who attacked her in the room hence why he knew the safe code was his own birthday, 3) Why end the story with Holli? Why not tell us about the actual plane people. We never did find out who they were., 4) I really thought she was going to end with an explanation that Mark knew the whole time and that's why they went out on the boat to find the location of the plane. And why he needed to see who was on it., 5) The couple who were killed at the resort wasn't explained very well, 6) I figured Mark being let go was all a cover story for this deal gone wrong and that explained his mood and crankiness. I still gave it 4 stars but now I am loving online conversations about it to see that I wasn't the only one with these questions. <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/48870567-jean"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1482907009i/48870567._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/48870567-jean">Jean</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    Sloppy characterization and a desire for a twist ending.<br /><br /><br />(Sorry, didn't realize you can't hide spoilers in questions, so SPOILER ALERT):<br /><br />We know Mark hi<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    Sloppy characterization and a desire for a twist ending.<br /><br /><br />(Sorry, didn't realize you can't hide spoilers in questions, so SPOILER ALERT):<br /><br />We know Mark hired Patrick to terrorize Erin and get her off the scent only a day or two after they got home from their honeymoon. That means there’s not time for any major change of heart on his part, whether it’s deeming Erin a liability or falling out of love with her.<br /><br />Presumably, the conclusion we’re meant to draw is that he never actually loved her, especially given this “look” he got in his eyes as he died. But that just raises more questions and makes the twist thinner: why marry her in the first place if you don’t love her? Is Mark meant to be a psychopath? Why don’t we see more psychopathic behavior from him, then? There certainly wasn’t enough in Mark’s behavior for me to buy that ending as believable.<br /><br />Personally, I’m well over this trend of authors trying to emulate Gone Girl without understanding why Gone Girl was so effective. Not everything needs a twist ending, especially one so shoddily supported by the story.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_2382482310" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2382482310" />
    <a title="Melissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9684061-melissa"><img alt="Melissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528750408p2/9684061.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2382482310?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/9684061-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=not-for-me">not-for-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=suspense-mystery-thriller">suspense-mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=too-much-hype">too-much-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=run-the-other-way">run-the-other-way</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9684061-melissa?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2382482310" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1025684261301149641"><blockquote>
  <i>Have you ever wondered how long it takes to dig a grave? Wonder no longer. It takes an age. However long you think it takes, double that.</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Let me start by giving credit where it’s due—<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16847770.Catherine_Steadman' title='Catherine Steadman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Catherine Steadman</a> <i>nails</i> the first chapter . . . hands down. Very few openers have acquired my attention as adeptly as those four simple sentences.<br/><br/>How could any suspense reader not be enthralled with a woman who turns to Google to learn the proper depth to bury a body or look away as she carries on, one painstaki</span>
  <span id="freeText1025684261301149641" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Have you ever wondered how long it takes to dig a grave? Wonder no longer. It takes an age. However long you think it takes, double that.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Let me start by giving credit where it’s due—<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16847770.Catherine_Steadman" title="Catherine Steadman" rel="nofollow noopener">Catherine Steadman</a> <i>nails</i> the first chapter . . . hands down. Very few openers have acquired my attention as adeptly as those four simple sentences.<br /><br />How could any suspense reader not be enthralled with a woman who turns to Google to learn the proper depth to bury a body or look away as she carries on, one painstaking shovel-full at a time? Erin proves with her narrative, ridding yourself of a pesky body, in dirt, might not be as easy as the movies portray. <i>*wink*</i><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I’m not a bad person. Or maybe I am. You decide.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />I think we can all agree—there’s not much subjectivity allowed here, is there?—<i>anyone</i> who finds themselves in a situation that requires the disposal of a body, pretty much guarantees they’re <u>not</u> a good person. What kind of reader would that make me though, if I didn’t give Erin the chance to explain herself? <br /><br />From Erin’s declaration on her moral character, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16847770.Catherine_Steadman" title="Catherine Steadman" rel="nofollow noopener">Catherine Steadman</a> flips the calendar back three months—setting to work the events that land her leading lady in the woods committing a major felony. <br /><br />Let me dip my toe in the plot here for a bit. Erin is a budding documentary filmmaker, while her soon to be husband, an investment banker, has recently found himself without a job. Less money means less of a fuss over their nuptials and a mere two weeks in Bora Bora, instead of the planned three. It’s in the turquoise waters off the island, in the midst of what anyone would consider a dream honeymoon, that the couple happens across <i>something</i> in the water. A few unfathomable items, just floating along, minding their own business, tucked securely away in a locked black bag. I think we’d all be kidding ourselves if we said we’d just leave it alone. What's that saying—<i>curiousity killed the cat?</i> The circumstances pose a bit of a moral dilemma, as they should; do Erin and Mark alert someone to what they found or shove the guilt down somewhere deep and live a more “prosperous” life, instead? Any guesses at the decision the couple makes?<br /><br />Things start to get a bit dicey when Erin and Mark find themselves back home in London, pretending to carry on as if nothing has changed. We all know, that scenario <i>never</i> holds up. What ensues is a non-stop decline in believability, a flagrant lack of storyline development and one absurd decision followed by another. From curiosity in the beginning, to waning feelings in the middle, to disdain for the crippling ridiculousness of the back half, this is one I’m labeling as a <i>major</i> upset. What kills me, this <s>could</s> should have been so much <i>more</i>.<br /><br />The entire story is told from Erin’s perspective and it’s my belief, the author’s writing style will be hit-or-miss with readers. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16847770.Catherine_Steadman" title="Catherine Steadman" rel="nofollow noopener">Catherine Steadman</a>’s words are <i>extremely</i> choppy, but in some ways, I felt her voice fed into the suspense of the novel and lessened the impact of the drivel. If you think about it, our own thoughts are far from linear and polished—there’s a rawness, a flitting from one thought to another . . . <i>constantly</i>. Well, that’s the best justification I can come up with for the messiness presented on the page.<br /><br />Was the story written this way intentionally? I’m not quite sure. What I am sure of, this story would have benefited from more editing. Quite a few times, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16847770.Catherine_Steadman" title="Catherine Steadman" rel="nofollow noopener">Catherine Steadman</a> wrote herself into a corner and continued to turn in circles, spewing bits of useless information, while trying to get back on track. Again, that’s just <i>my</i> take on the steady diet of nonsense the author chose to spoon-feed the reader.<br /><br />I'm going to end things on this note: when writing a story, or heck, even in real life, simply <i>thinking</i> about something, doesn’t necessarily breath it in to fruition—regardless of how many times this plot tries to persuade you otherwise. If that was the case, the ending of this book would have been something else entirely. <br /><br /><i>***Thank you to Ballantine Books and NetGalley for providing a review copy.***</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1025684261301149641" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2426472849" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2426472849" />
    <a title="Ova - Excuse My Reading" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5316099-ova---excuse-my-reading"><img alt="Ova - Excuse My Reading" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543876995p2/5316099.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2426472849?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ova - Excuse My Reading" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ova - Excuse My Reading" href="/user/show/5316099-ova---excuse-my-reading">Ova - Excuse My Reading</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5316099-ova---excuse-my-reading?shelf=avoid-at-all-costs">avoid-at-all-costs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2426472849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10540244221455328000"><a href='https://excusemyreading.com/2018/07/06/something-in-the-water-oh-wait-its-frustration/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Full review here</a><br/>This might seem harsh but I really don't understand how this book got published in the way it is.<br/><br/>THIS REVIEW CONTAINS SPOILERS.<br/><br/><b>STYLE AND WRITING</b><br/><br/>Steadman’s writing, is not steady. Well. There is A LOT in this book. A LOT. In the beginning I thought: hey, she must be going into these details for a reason. Then the more I read, the more I became sure: there is no reason for us reading a wedding reception 3 course menu, and prices, for pages, OR how our character interprets a pregnan</span>
  <span id="freeText10540244221455328000" style="display:none"><a href="https://excusemyreading.com/2018/07/06/something-in-the-water-oh-wait-its-frustration/" rel="nofollow noopener">Full review here</a><br />This might seem harsh but I really don't understand how this book got published in the way it is.<br /><br />THIS REVIEW CONTAINS SPOILERS.<br /><br /><b>STYLE AND WRITING</b><br /><br />Steadman’s writing, is not steady. Well. There is A LOT in this book. A LOT. In the beginning I thought: hey, she must be going into these details for a reason. Then the more I read, the more I became sure: there is no reason for us reading a wedding reception 3 course menu, and prices, for pages, OR how our character interprets a pregnancy test for at least a few page (I mean not emotionally but literally with the blue crosses and a lot of ‘fuck’ and ‘shits’),OR how do we learn about Glock’s for at least 5 pages – at that point I asked myself, I can read this in Wikipedia-Honestly, as far as I know it’s better to tell something with less words. I can edit this book and cut it to half of it’s size, EASILY without losing anything in the plot at all. Steadman literally talks about everything in this book. The character boards onto a plane and we have a lecture about first classes. The character dives into sea and we have a lecture and description about different types of sharks. There is a lot more. Just asking: WHY? WHAT THE HELL? Do people really enjoy reading these, hence so many 5 stars?<br /><br /><b>THE PLOT</b><br /><br />I won’t lie. The first 30% wasn’t that bad. Then it just started tumbling down to the cliff into the water!<br />The plot is absurd. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Our protagonist, Erin is engaged with an investment banker, Mark, who mysteriously gets fired from his high-paying job days before their wedding. They go to honeymoon. They find SOMETHING in the water. Then hell breaks lose. It’s alright. Erin is an idiot, I understand. Mark is as flat as an A4 paper but he does the job. Then there is a whole storyline of 3 prisoners, Holli, Eddie and Alexa. Erin meets and interviews them to make a documentary and it looks like they’re just thrown in to spice it up. Oh wait, one of the prisoners, Eddie the dangerous criminal, becomes Erin’s fairy-gangsta-mother, so that must be why they’re in. Every time Erin has a criminal problem, she rings Eddie. Uh, oh, I think HMP Pentonville must be operating as a call center. I can’t see how else Eddie can take so many calls from Erin. So here is a tip, if you have a body to dispose, some illegal diamonds to sell, you ever need a gun, or encrypt some illegal documents, I don’t know, just ring HMP Pentonville and I am sure they can put in contact with the right sort of criminal.There are so many silly things about the plot that makes your eyes roll : like Mark and Erin smuggling loads of diamonds and millions of dollars to the UK without any problems in their luggage- which I honestly think British Border Force should take as a wake up call if this is the case with first class passengers never being searched-, or Erin trying to sell the diamonds almost in the open market next to vegetables and the criminals still can’t spot them, silly criminals…Did I mention Holli suddenly running wild to Isis- what the heck was this for we’ll never know) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /> It felt like Steadman had a wild dream and decided to write this into a novel.<br /><br /><b>THE INATTENTION TO DETAIL</b><br /><br />I am very frustrated to the fact that Steadman (and the editor ) never realised these mistakes about Turkey / Turkish in the book. First Gaziantep, a big city in Turkey with nearly 2 million inhabitants is told as : "a small village". Yes, with this exact words. <br />Also Steadman invents a Turkish guy called Ashar Farooq. Which is CLEARLY Arabic. I found this very offensive, to be honest. Turks and Arabs don't share a language and a culture. They share a religion in a way Catholics and Protestants share theirs. This is a bit like saying: Oh well, if these countries are next to each other, why not. Who cares it's a Turkish or Arabic name/man, they're all the same. <br /><br /><b>Verdict:</b><br /><br />1 star. Will I read again from Steadman? No. #SorryNotSorry<br /><br />Thanks for Netgalley and publisher for a free copy of the book in exchange for an honest review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10540244221455328000" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2391231333" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2391231333" />
    <a title="Mackenzie - PhDiva Books" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57632045-mackenzie---phdiva-books"><img alt="Mackenzie - PhDiva Books" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562505567p2/57632045.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2391231333?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mackenzie - PhDiva Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mackenzie - PhDiva Books" href="/user/show/57632045-mackenzie---phdiva-books">Mackenzie - PhDiva Books</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57632045-mackenzie---phdiva-books?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57632045-mackenzie---phdiva-books?shelf=2018-psychological-thrillers">2018-psychological-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57632045-mackenzie---phdiva-books?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2391231333" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8356970424621671752">5 <i>THUNK THUNK THUNK</i> Stars 🌟🌟🌟🌟🌟!!!<br/><br/>A slow build to a shocking discovery, this book will have you wondering what you would do!!! See my review <a href='https://phdiva.blog/2018/05/20/review-something-in-the-water/' rel='nofollow noopener'>here!</a><br/><br/>What an incredible debut novel this is for Catherine Steadman! While the book starts with a bang, the next 30% is a slow build as you get to know the characters. Then at about 35% the story takes a turn and readers will find themselves holding on for the ride, unsure of where they’ll end up!!! I was unsure about this book at first, but I have to say I </span>
  <span id="freeText8356970424621671752" style="display:none">5 <i>THUNK THUNK THUNK</i> Stars 🌟🌟🌟🌟🌟!!!<br /><br />A slow build to a shocking discovery, this book will have you wondering what you would do!!! See my review <a href="https://phdiva.blog/2018/05/20/review-something-in-the-water/" rel="nofollow noopener">here!</a><br /><br />What an incredible debut novel this is for Catherine Steadman! While the book starts with a bang, the next 30% is a slow build as you get to know the characters. Then at about 35% the story takes a turn and readers will find themselves holding on for the ride, unsure of where they’ll end up!!! I was unsure about this book at first, but I have to say I ended up really enjoying it and found it to be a tantalizing premise for a story. <br /><br />I don’t even know what I’d compare this book to… Its really quite unique from other psychological thrillers, though I’m sure some comparisons (Ruth Ware, Paula Hawkins) are bound to come up. I don’t want to make those though because I don’t think readers should go into this book expecting something similar to what they’ve already read. Enjoy this one on it’s own merit!<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Erin and Mark are about to embark on their dream honeymoon...</i>
</b><br /><br />Erin is a documentary filmmaker and is engaged to handsome, successful, financial advisor Mark. The two have a nearly perfect relationship—each balances the other out, and is able to cheer the other up when down. Erin is creating a documentary about prisoners reintegrating into society after their release, when she takes a break and she and Mark leave grey-skied England for a dream honeymoon in Bora Bora.<br /><br />Mark and Erin spend their days hiking, eating exotic meals, basking in the sun, and making love in their room—a perfect honeymoon! Erin is even facing her fear of scuba diving to see the oceans with Mark. But after a big storm makes the waters cloudy, they are forced to change their dive location to a different island about an hour off the shore of Bora Bora.<br /><br /><i>And then, out in a boat in the middle of the ocean, they hear it....</i><br /><br /><b>THUNK THUNK THUNK<br /><br /><i>There’s something in the water, and nothing will ever be the same again…</i></b><br /><br />I cannot believe this is a debut novel! Catherine has a way with vivid characters, settings, and vernacular, probably from her career as an actress. I found Erin and Mark so compelling, both as individuals and in their relationship dynamic. Mark is calculating where Erin is creative. Erin is action-oriented where Mark is strategic. Both are open to understanding when they’ve misunderstood the other.<br /><br />But I don’t want to forget to mention the other characters! The three prisoners—Holli, Alexa, and Eddie—are fascinating each in their own way. Steadman shows the incredible diversity of those who are convicted. Some may deserve worse than they got, and others you might empathize with, or even see a bit of your own decision-making in. Each has their own story, peppered throughout the book in Erin’s interviews with them.<br /><br />And the mystery!!! The “something” that is in the water!!! It sets a chain of events in motion that are twisty and heart-pounding in their rapid succession. From the time the boat hits the <i>THUNK THUNK</i>, readers will NOT be able to put this book down! Erin and Mark both handle the situation so differently. Erin surprises even herself with her boldness, which was wonderful to read about. Erin was a great narrator, even if I did want to shake her at times and tell her to stop, JUST STOP!<br /><br />The series of tiny decisions that could lead them on different paths each step of the way was extremely well-written. I found myself unsure at each stage what I would choose. Would I follow the same path that Erin and Mark did? What would I do, if I were the one to find something in the water? I wanted to avoid saying much about the plot beyond the discovery, because readers will absolutely love the ride this book will take them on! I look forward to more from this author.<br /><br />I want to sincerely thank Netgalley, Catherine Steadman, and Ballantine Books at Random House Publishing for an opportunity to read this book in exchange for an honest review. It was my pleasure!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8356970424621671752" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14714394897754629958"><b> 5 Tension Filled Stars 🌟🌟🌟🌟🌟</b><br/><br/>Well HOT damn this book was just... brilliant! Full disclosure I was running behind on my reviews so I purchased this on audio on release day and I was even a little hesitant because I saw the author was narrating.... not always a good thing, but I had no idea that Catherine Steadman is an actress.... and after finishing this book I now know she is also a fantastic author and audiobook narrator!!! Simply amazing! Seriously if I could I would give her narration six st</span>
  <span id="freeText14714394897754629958" style="display:none"><b> 5 Tension Filled Stars 🌟🌟🌟🌟🌟</b><br /><br />Well HOT damn this book was just... brilliant! Full disclosure I was running behind on my reviews so I purchased this on audio on release day and I was even a little hesitant because I saw the author was narrating.... not always a good thing, but I had no idea that Catherine Steadman is an actress.... and after finishing this book I now know she is also a fantastic author and audiobook narrator!!! Simply amazing! Seriously if I could I would give her narration six stars, it was really exceptional! And this book kept me on the edge of my seat from about 30% on...<br /><br />Erin and Mark are a happy newly married couple on their honeymoon in Bora Bora... they are having a wonderful time in this tropical paradise until...thunk thunk... there is something in the water.... and what it is will alter this couple’s lives.... from this point on the tension is ramped up and I felt as though I was on the edge of my seat throughout... so many thoughts... what would I do in this situation? What is the ethical thing to do?<br /><br />Erin and Mark were both fabulous characters... they both handled the situation so differently and I found that part so compelling and true....Erin was very bold about it all and didn’t always think things through, in fact sometimes she did some really stupid things... Mark on the other hand was more cautious, not much of a risk taker, although he was usually fine with his wife taking a risk.... I have to say I was both surprised and a little disappointed by both of these characters at points in this book....<br /><br />There is also a very fascinating side story in this book... Erin is filming a documentary about prisoners about to be released.... Eddie, Holly, and Alexa were all strong, interesting, and well-developed characters.... I found each of their storys compelling and unique.... definitely added another layer to this already wonderful book.... and the voice of eddie is absolutely the best in this audio!<br /><br />This really was a book unlike any other I have read before... it was very refreshing.... absolutely recommend to everybody regardless of your reading preferences!<br /><br />*** thank you to the publisher for my copy of this brilliant book ***</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17618539087569381648">I had a really hard time rating this one.... do you ever have books where you get so frustrated with the characters that you just want to scream? Well.. this is definitely one where I was super frustrated and wanted to throw my kindle at times lol. <br/><br/>Erin and Mark are a newly married couple that don't have the best honest relationship. I noticed that Erin and Mark both have been keeping secrets from one another. Erin is trusting Mark a little more then she should despite all the red flags. But, Er</span>
  <span id="freeText17618539087569381648" style="display:none">I had a really hard time rating this one.... do you ever have books where you get so frustrated with the characters that you just want to scream? Well.. this is definitely one where I was super frustrated and wanted to throw my kindle at times lol. <br /><br />Erin and Mark are a newly married couple that don't have the best honest relationship. I noticed that Erin and Mark both have been keeping secrets from one another. Erin is trusting Mark a little more then she should despite all the red flags. But, Erin isn't so innocent either and has been keeping just as much from her husband Mark. Seems like a disaster waiting to happen..eeek! <br /><br />Erin is a filmmaker who has an interest in the world of crime. She begins a filming project about three people who are being released from prison. The documentary examines closely the lives of these three individuals and starts out as a project but ends up taking a sinister turn. While on their honeymoon, Mark and Erin find a mysterious black bag in the ocean. Let's just say... the items in the bag are not in the least bit innocent. This of course.... adds intense moments and leads to a show of an ending. <br /><br />I had some issues with this book which is why I only gave it three stars. One, my god was this book slow up until 50 percent for me. I felt like nothing was happening and I was struggling to complete chapter after chapter. Finally it picked up half way through! I felt that some of the events that transpired from Mark and Erin's decisions were just too unbelievable. I felt that it would be almost impossible to get away with some of the things that Mark and Erin got away with. Too much security etc currently. <br /><br />I feel like this was an overall average thriller for me with a decent ending :).<br /><br />3 stars<br /><br />Thank you so much to Netgalley and Random House Ballantine for an advanced arc in exchange for my honest review. <br /><br />Published to GR: 5/23/18<br />Publication date: 6/5/18</span>

<div id="review_2418062898" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2418062898" />
    <a title="j e w e l s" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s"><img alt="j e w e l s" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552606306p2/68216634.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2418062898?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="j e w e l s" class="user" itemprop="url" name="j e w e l s" href="/user/show/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s">j e w e l s</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/40390080-something-in-the-water">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s?shelf=twister-hall-of-fame">twister-hall-of-fame</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s?shelf=books-bejeweled">books-bejeweled</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68216634-j-e-w-e-l-s?shelf=audio">audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2418062898" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15022654010281855395"><b>FIVE STARS</b><br/><br/>For domestic suspense fun, it doesn't get much better than this! <b>SOMETHING IN THE WATER</b> is<i> Numero Uno</i> on the NYT bestseller list this week, a Reese's bookclub selection and the movie rights have long been snatched up! <br/><br/>All that buzzy attention heaped on one <b>lil ole debut novel </b>can make some of us (okay.....me😂)a tad skeptical. No need to worry. You are in expert hands with Catherine Steadman. Maybe you live on a deserted island and haven't heard, but Steadman is a fabulous, gorgeous act</span>
  <span id="freeText15022654010281855395" style="display:none"><b>FIVE STARS</b><br /><br />For domestic suspense fun, it doesn't get much better than this! <b>SOMETHING IN THE WATER</b> is<i> Numero Uno</i> on the NYT bestseller list this week, a Reese's bookclub selection and the movie rights have long been snatched up! <br /><br />All that buzzy attention heaped on one <b>lil ole debut novel </b>can make some of us (okay.....me😂)a tad skeptical. No need to worry. You are in expert hands with Catherine Steadman. Maybe you live on a deserted island and haven't heard, but Steadman is a fabulous, gorgeous actress working in the U.K. She, most notably, was a cast member of Britain's Downton Abbey. She can also write like the pros, if not better. What the heck? So much talent in one person! Quit your day job or not, Ms. Steadman, you are a superstar either way!<br /><br />There are tons of summaries out there. Please don't read them. Listen, I accidentally read the "spoilest spoilers" EVER in the New York Times and Kirkus Reviews. Geez. Don't look for more about the story. I would have enjoyed it so much more if I didn't already know <u>what</u> the <i>something in the water</i> was! Take my word for it.<br /><br /><b>The pacing is brisk, the narrator is unreliable (<i>BUT NOT A DRUNK!</i>) and the story translates quite believably as a realistic situation. You guys know how much I abhor the hand-wringing heroine. But here, our protagonist is VERY pro-action. True, she doesn't always make the best decisions (omg!), but she tries her best and I, for one, felt a weird kind of kinship with our main character.</b> <br /><br />It's my favorite kind of suspense-building story. One bad decision leads to another, leads to one more and so on.....It's the ultimate "what would you do" situational structure. Steadman writes in a slick, sophisticated manner. I'm completely infatuated with her wit and style.<br /><br /><b>If you enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22557272.The_Girl_on_the_Train" title="The Girl on the Train by Paula Hawkins" rel="nofollow noopener">The Girl on the Train</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28187230.The_Woman_in_Cabin_10" title="The Woman in Cabin 10 by Ruth Ware" rel="nofollow noopener">The Woman in Cabin 10</a>, or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/35506211.The_Flight_Attendant" title="The Flight Attendant by Chris Bohjalian" rel="nofollow noopener">The Flight Attendant</a> you will love <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36388243.Something_in_the_Water" title="Something in the Water by Catherine Steadman" rel="nofollow noopener">Something in the Water</a>.</b><br /><br /><i>The audiobook is stellar! Steadman acts as her own icy, sexy narrator and you will quickly understand why she is such a wonderful actress! Highly recommend! I am so excited to discover this new, gifted author. Looking forward to her career in this difficult-to-write genre.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="15022654010281855395" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2388789827" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2388789827" />
    <a title="Julie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5210022-julie"><img alt="Julie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356906542p2/5210022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2388789827?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie " href="/user/show/5210022-julie">Julie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2388789827" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6278249793891437116">Something in the Water by Catherine Steadman is a 2018 Ballantine publication. <br/><br/> Slightly predictable morality tale with a nice hook and a few clever twists-<br/><br/>You just got married, you’re in financial straits, looking at a drastic change in your quality of living standards, but you’ve already got a nice honeymoon planned in Bora Bora- so why not enjoy every minute of your vacation? That's what newlyweds Erin and Mark plan on doing before they head back to reality and an uncertain future. <br/><br/>But, on a </span>
  <span id="freeText6278249793891437116" style="display:none">Something in the Water by Catherine Steadman is a 2018 Ballantine publication. <br /><br /> Slightly predictable morality tale with a nice hook and a few clever twists-<br /><br />You just got married, you’re in financial straits, looking at a drastic change in your quality of living standards, but you’ve already got a nice honeymoon planned in Bora Bora- so why not enjoy every minute of your vacation? That's what newlyweds Erin and Mark plan on doing before they head back to reality and an uncertain future. <br /><br />But, on a standard scuba dive they discover something in the water, a discovery that puts them in a very prickly position. However, the bottom line is they probably hit the Motherload. But, they also make another, very grisly discovery, and in their paranoid horror and glee, make a few whopping mistakes that could come back to haunt them. <br /><br />Can they get away with keeping something that doesn’t belong to them? Should they? What if someone finds out?<br /><br /> The pressure they were under before is nothing like the pressure they are under now. As they work to cover all their bases, they face one moral dilemma after another, as lies and rationalizations take over and they slide further into moral bankruptcy every day.<br /> <br />Erin, a documentary filmmaker, is our narrator, laying out the full story going back to when she and Mark first met. Mark’s job as an investment banker, ended abruptly and quite unexpectedly, forcing Mark to face the dismal prospect of having to take any job he can find, in an economic downturn. <br /><br />The treasure they find is the answer to all their problems, but they aren't prepared for the lengths they will have to go to to profit from their discoveries, while trying not to get caught. They soon find themselves rubbing elbows with less than trustworthy people, justifying their moral compromises and keeping secrets from each other. <br /><br /><br />Right now, psychological thrillers are so popular publishers are rushing subpar novels with interchangeable plotlines into the marketplace in record numbers.<br /><br /> It’s so bad I’ve begun removing PTs from my TBR pile, before I burn out completely. ( Sort of reminds me of the fever pitch PNR and Urban Fantasy reached back at the peak of 'Twilight's' popularity- thank God that's over! Maybe Fifty Shades of Grey knockoffs are on the way out too- one can only hope!) But- I digress. <br /><br /><br />This book, however, had a very intriguing synopsis and the ratings were mostly favorable, so I had to see why it was popular. While I was hopeful, I also approached the book with cautious optimism.<br /> <br />Thankfully, despite my having picked up on a few ‘tells’ early on in the novel, I found myself caught up more in the character’s fear, guilt and self-loathing, their guilty consciences- or lack thereof- battling against the need to cover their butts and pull off the caper of the century, all so they can maintain a lifestyle they had grown accustomed to. It was an interesting journey, from that standpoint. The parallels between Erin’s documentary subjects and her own life didn’t go unnoticed and the role they played in the story was ironic. <br /><br />However, the characters were often so naïve, so utterly clueless, I wanted to scream- or maybe I didn't give them enough credit. You’ll have to be the judge on that one. <br /><br />Overall, the story is a little predictable, but I was very engaged, and very interested to see how everything would turn out in the end. It’s an addictive read, with some well- timed twists, that are every effective. Overall, I ended up enjoying this one for the most part. It has a few flaws but didn’t feel like a book written just to cash in on a trend. Perhaps, Steadman will try her hand at this more often- in between her acting roles, of course. <br /><br />4 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="6278249793891437116" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18109675738100999180"><b>🌠🌠🌠🌠🌠 Chilling, Thrilling, and Killing Stars!</b><br/><br/><br/>My rating system is very simple. If I read a book straight through the night, can't put it down at work, interrupt meals to get back to it, it's worthy of five stars. And this was the case for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36388243.Something_in_the_Water' title='Something in the Water by Catherine Steadman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Something in the Water</a>. <s>Very few books</s>, achem, thrillers deserve five stars, imho. They are either lacking in character development, plot development or a mixture of the two. I thought this thriller was expertly plotted and quick-paced. Although I found the begi</span>
  <span id="freeText18109675738100999180" style="display:none"><b>🌠🌠🌠🌠🌠 Chilling, Thrilling, and Killing Stars!</b><br><br><br>My rating system is very simple. If I read a book straight through the night, can't put it down at work, interrupt meals to get back to it, it's worthy of five stars. And this was the case for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36388243.Something_in_the_Water" title="Something in the Water by Catherine Steadman" rel="nofollow noopener">Something in the Water</a>. <s>Very few books</s>, achem, thrillers deserve five stars, imho. They are either lacking in character development, plot development or a mixture of the two. I thought this thriller was expertly plotted and quick-paced. Although I found the beginning to be a little odd, it does make sense within the larger context of the book. <br><br>What is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36388243.Something_in_the_Water" title="Something in the Water by Catherine Steadman" rel="nofollow noopener">Something in the Water</a> about? A couple, Erin and Mark, having just gotten married, set forth on their honeymoon in Bora, Bora. Although, instead of having a relaxing vacation on the beach they find a shocking discovery that upends their entire life. I'm not going to say anymore, you'll just have to read the book!<br><br>This was a buddy read for me and it made my enjoyment of the book even greater. As my reading buddy pointed out, you'll have to suspend your belief in sections of this novel. There are definitely moments that are too coincidental or where the protagonist is just "too lucky." This didn't bother me, but if you are a skeptical reader, it might.<br><br>All in all, I found this to be extremely fun. I could easily equate this with a roller coaster, having so many twists and turns. I couldn't put it down, and for me, that is the mark of <b>killer thriller</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496819675ra/22954519.gif" width="380" height="348" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Thank you to the publisher for providing me with an ARC in exchange for review </i></span>

<div id="review_2380016140" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2380016140" />
    <a title="Mischenko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1194517-mischenko"><img alt="Mischenko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587209348p2/1194517.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2380016140?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mischenko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mischenko" href="/user/show/1194517-mischenko">Mischenko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/40390080-something-in-the-water">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2380016140" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1262723222496375594">I love psychological thrillers, so when I saw this on Audible I gave it a shot. I love that the book is narrated by the author. I thought she was perfect and had no issues there. The story just sort of fell flat for me.<br/><br/>The two main characters are Erin and Mark and the book is told from Erin’s POV. Erin writes documentaries for a living, while her husband Mark is an investment banker. He’s handsome and super loved by everyone. They’re newlyweds–very much in love– and about to head on an extravaga</span>
  <span id="freeText1262723222496375594" style="display:none">I love psychological thrillers, so when I saw this on Audible I gave it a shot. I love that the book is narrated by the author. I thought she was perfect and had no issues there. The story just sort of fell flat for me.<br /><br />The two main characters are Erin and Mark and the book is told from Erin’s POV. Erin writes documentaries for a living, while her husband Mark is an investment banker. He’s handsome and super loved by everyone. They’re newlyweds–very much in love– and about to head on an extravagant honeymoon. Plans to have a family are on the horizon. While scuba diving in Bora Bora, they discover something in the water that has the potential to change their lives forever. It becomes clear fairly quickly that they’ve gotten themselves into a boat-load of trouble.<br /><br />One decision after another; they seem to have it all planned out. The problem is that sometimes Erin’s curiosity gets the best of her and it was times like this where I just cringed. I almost couldn’t take it! There were parts in the book where I just couldn’t stand her character and wanted to scream. It’s these events, however, that move the plot along and make it interesting. Not only that, Mark can be a jerk when he wants to be and I had a hard time figuring him out in the beginning. The question is, can they stick together and really pull this off? If it weren’t for the <b>HUGE</b> spoiler in the beginning of the book, it might not be so easy to figure out.<br /><br />After the first big introduction, the book starts out slow and boring and gradually just keeps getting better. For me though, it fell flat–probably because of the way it started and knowing a crucial detail from the very start. I’m iffy about beginnings like that, although you’re left to wonder about Erin’s character throughout because of it. The ending was fairly predictable and I could see where it was going though.<br /><br />One of my biggest issues with the book was all the added details and some of the secondary characters. I just found them sort of worthless and they took away from the main plot. With that said, I did still enjoy the book and there were a few times where I was on edge. I was very anxious a few times in the story. It just wasn’t as thrilling as I expected it to be. If you like thrillers, I would still recommend you give this one a try!<br /><br />3***<br /><br />See this review on my blog @ <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://readrantrockandroll.com/2018/10/17/book-review-something-in-the-water-by-catherine-steadman-audible/">https://readrantrockandroll.com/2018/...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1262723222496375594" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2409611202" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2409611202" />
    <a title="JanB " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/260116-janb"><img alt="JanB " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527313486p2/260116.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2409611202?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="JanB " class="user" itemprop="url" name="JanB " href="/user/show/260116-janb">JanB </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2409611202" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8556294332134298311">First the positives: The author narrates the audiobook and she does a fabulous job. The story opens with a great line: “Have you ever wondered how long it takes to dig a grave? Wonder no longer. It takes an age. However long you think it takes, double that.” <br/><br/>With that line I was hooked. Until I read/listened to roughly 10 pages of details about the intricacies and details of digging a grave, including the cubic feet of the hole, and how much the soil weighs. Which, in case you are wondering, is </span>
  <span id="freeText8556294332134298311" style="display:none">First the positives: The author narrates the audiobook and she does a fabulous job. The story opens with a great line: “Have you ever wondered how long it takes to dig a grave? Wonder no longer. It takes an age. However long you think it takes, double that.” <br /><br />With that line I was hooked. Until I read/listened to roughly 10 pages of details about the intricacies and details of digging a grave, including the cubic feet of the hole, and how much the soil weighs. Which, in case you are wondering, is 36 cubic feet and 1.5 tons, the size of a beluga whale or hippo. But who cares???<br /><br />Knowing the protagonist actually had the wherewithal to google how to dig a grave made me think she was a sociopath. Who would stop to google how to dig a grave when you're burying your husband after a series of shocking events?? So right off, I know Erin is either a sociopath, dumb as a box of rocks, and analyzes EVERYTHING, or maybe all three. And when I say she analyzes everything I mean everything. You, the reader, get to hear all about it. Incessantly. With details that do not further the plot or matter one whit to what is happening.<br /><br />From the grave digging scene we travel back in time to find how they got to this point. Erin and Mark are deeply in love (so we are repeatedly told) and planning their wedding with a 3 week honeymoon to Bora Bora. But Mark just lost his job as an investment banker and all potential job prospects have dried up. Erin is shocked when Mark has to spell out in detail that the loss of his job means they will have to cut back on the wedding. This is further confirmation that Erin is stupendously stupid. After the wedding they fly first class to Bora Bora but “economize” by staying 2 weeks instead of 3. No mention of how they will pay the mortgage on their $1.5 million dollar home.<br /><br />But, Ok, I kept reading thinking this would get better. Plus I really wanted to know what it was they found in the water. It was a very slow build until it was finally revealed. Unfortunately, it was anticlimactic and things went furhter downhill from here. After the discovery, the only thing that drives the plot forward is a series of incredibly stupid decisions. <br /><br />Erin narrates the story and it is often filled with completely irrelevant details that looked like a Wikipedia cut and paste job. For instance, she tells you all you never wanted to know about Glocks…WHY was this included? Filler, that's why. And she never uses a few words when she can drag out the simple act of turning on a phone to an entire paragraph. <br /><br />Some characters are introduced that have no purpose to the story while the characters who matter are not developed enough to explain the “twist” when it comes. There are inconsistencies and plot holes that are never explained. <br /><br /> The premise is a good one. It has been done before but it held potential. With a good enough editor and some re-writes this could have been a much better book.<br /><br /> There are plenty of 4 and 5 star reviews out there and I am apparently an outlier. <br /><br />Bottom line: skip it. But I finished it so it gets 2 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8556294332134298311" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2296827530" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2296827530" />
    <a title="Linda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9472704-linda"><img alt="Linda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1336837712p2/9472704.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2296827530?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda" href="/user/show/9472704-linda">Linda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9472704-linda?shelf=mystery-thrillers">mystery-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9472704-linda?shelf=net-galley">net-galley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2296827530" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer815615060765152617">Step back from the flame, honey. <br/><br/>You're gonna get burned.<br/><br/>Mark and Erin are on a stellar honeymoon in Bora Bora. Sun, sea, and each other. She's a documentary film producer and he's a successful investment banker. No worries. Or so it seems until they find something floating in the water. The depth of that ocean pales in comparison to the depth of problems that are gonna follow this couple home like stink on the back of a wayward skunk. <br/><br/>How deep is deep enough?<br/><br/>Catherine Steadman creates quite the</span>
  <span id="freeText815615060765152617" style="display:none">Step back from the flame, honey. <br /><br />You're gonna get burned.<br /><br />Mark and Erin are on a stellar honeymoon in Bora Bora. Sun, sea, and each other. She's a documentary film producer and he's a successful investment banker. No worries. Or so it seems until they find something floating in the water. The depth of that ocean pales in comparison to the depth of problems that are gonna follow this couple home like stink on the back of a wayward skunk. <br /><br />How deep is deep enough?<br /><br />Catherine Steadman creates quite the electrically charged happenings in Something In The Water. The opening scene finds our lovely Erin digging someone's grave. She quickly adjusts her calculations from the usual 6-footer job. A little lady can only do so much.<br /><br />Steadman ratchets her storyline back a few months to where Erin is setting up her latest documentary commitment within the walls of Pentonville Prison. Erin and her camerman will follow the lives of three individuals before and after their release. Face-to-face interviews are going to leave their mark not only for the intended audience but heavily upon Erin herself. We, as readers, are going to remember their faces as well.<br /><br />Just keep in mind your usual response in a darkened movie theater to the girl who has her hand on the doorknob: Don't, please don't, go down in that creepy basement alone, sweetheart. There's bad, bad things waiting for you in the shadows......so much more than just spiders hunched over in their webs. We're talkin' the two legged kind that mean serious business. And Erin is going to find out the hard way what that's all about even before the web is spun.<br /><br />I've got to hand it to Catherine Steadman for keeping the tension on high voltage throughout this one. You'll probably be smacking the book alongside the spine just to take out your frustration at what our girl is going to be up to. This is a fast-paced, believe-it-or-not trip from the lapping waves of Bora Bora to the hard reality of North London. But well worth the flight, dear readers. Well worth the flight.<br /><br />I received a copy of Something In The Water through NetGalley for an honest review. My thanks to Random House and to Catherine Steadman for the opportunity.<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="815615060765152617" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2198992708" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2198992708" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31923026-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533734143p2/31923026.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2198992708?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/31923026-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=crime-mystery-thriller">crime-mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2198992708" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13624373241038637113"><blockquote>
  <i>Have you ever wondered how long it takes to dig a grave? Wonder no longer. It takes an age. However long you think it takes, double that.</i>
</blockquote><br/>And with an opening sentence like that, I was in. I cannot deny that the suspense build was good here and certainly had me glued to the pages in front of me. I was desperate to know what it is this passionately in love couple found in the water on their honeymoon in Bora Bora that would set them on this course of destruction. The issue is: the payoff of tha</span>
  <span id="freeText13624373241038637113" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Have you ever wondered how long it takes to dig a grave? Wonder no longer. It takes an age. However long you think it takes, double that.</i>
</blockquote><br />And with an opening sentence like that, I was in. I cannot deny that the suspense build was good here and certainly had me glued to the pages in front of me. I was desperate to know what it is this passionately in love couple found in the water on their honeymoon in Bora Bora that would set them on this course of destruction. The issue is: the payoff of that awesome suspense build-up was nonexistent. The big twist was predictable. And the random tangents the narrator would go off on to give paragraphs of information that is completely irrelevant to the plot at hand...<br /><br />I should've known this would be a thing when the detail of what it takes to dig a grave in that first chapter was so elaborate that I could've then gone to dig a grave myself without needing to google any of the specifications including depth necessary to be successful. I copped it to a build of suspense..because who isn't intrigued by an opening chapter where a woman is digging a grave and gets into the intricacies of what needs to be done. I figured the author was painting a picture of a desperate woman completely out of her element just doing what she needs to in order to resolve the insane situation she's found herself in. Makes sense, right? The thing is..the author could've done this without all that added irrelevant detail. Steadman does this again later on a specific kind of gun with so much detail. I don't even understand why it was included. It felt like I was reading the handbook that came with the gun. None of it mattered to the plot at all. In fact, only one small detail did. And it didn't need to be thrown in with a bunch of useless, unimportant facts to make sure we knew about it. The writing felt sloppy when it came to this.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>Oh fucking hell. Those two constantly tugging needs: your own life and “being there.” Your relationship or your life. No matter how hard you try, you can’t have both.</i>
</blockquote><br />I kept reading in hopes of a big pay-off or blow-your-mind kind of twist, but that never happened. What I did love was the detail that went into traveling to Bora Bora with all the connecting flights and whatnot. And the vacation itself was intriguing. This is where I truly appreciated the detail that bothered me otherwise. And maybe it's that I find traveling interesting as opposed to guns or digging holes. I know besides the setting change, all the detail about the flights and resort are just unnecessary. But these were my favorite parts of the book. &amp; that has nothing to do with that something being found in the water in Bora Bora.<br /><br />Somehow throughout the hubbub of detail, Steadman still managed to keep me intrigued enough by the mystery. Although it wasn't hard to know when you 100% should not trust a character. It also didn't make sense that at times the characters were very smart about handling things, but at others seemed to lack all common sense. It's unfortunate because this could've been so much better..</span>
  <a data-text-id="13624373241038637113" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2421705236?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Holly  B (semi-hiatus until Jan)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Holly  B (semi-hiatus until Jan)" href="/user/show/39749481-holly-b-semi-hiatus-until-jan">Holly  B (semi-hiatus until Jan)</a>

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2421705236" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1828506581789386542"><em>
  <strong>This one starts with a bang!</strong>
</em><br/><br/>The opening chapter was one of the most intriguing I've read in a very long time. I was instantly curious and wanted to know what happened ( <em>an event in </em><em>the end of the story is revealed in the beginning chapter).  </em>Let's just say I was <em>
  <strong>hooked!</strong>
</em><br/><br/>I listened to this one on Audible and the narrator (<em>who happens to be the author Catherine Steadman ) </em>was perfection.  The timeline shifts back to tell the story of Erin and Mark, who are newlyweds, passionately in love an</span>
  <span id="freeText1828506581789386542" style="display:none"><em>
  <strong>This one starts with a bang!</strong>
</em><br /><br />The opening chapter was one of the most intriguing I've read in a very long time. I was instantly curious and wanted to know what happened ( <em>an event in </em><em>the end of the story is revealed in the beginning chapter).  </em>Let's just say I was <em>
  <strong>hooked!</strong>
</em><br /><br />I listened to this one on Audible and the narrator (<em>who happens to be the author Catherine Steadman ) </em>was perfection.  The timeline shifts back to tell the story of Erin and Mark, who are newlyweds, passionately in love and planning a trip in the sun to Bora, Bora.  Sunbathing, scuba diving, champagne drinking. <strong>What could possibly go wrong? </strong>Well, turns out plenty.<br /><br />I loved the unreliable characters, the twisty edge of your seat plot, and rather frantic pace.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1828506581789386542" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2334967618" />
    <a title="megs_bookrack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack"><img alt="megs_bookrack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532027727p2/48328025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2334967618?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="megs_bookrack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="megs_bookrack" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack">megs_bookrack</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48328025-megs-bookrack?shelf=arcs-read">arcs-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2334967618" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2445707922297204372"><b>**3.5-stars**</b><br/><br/>A solid Summer read! <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491417804ra/22408909.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>Something in the Water</i> starts in a very peculiar place, quickly drawing me into the story.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1524417499ra/25416681.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>In contrast to a lot of what I am reading lately, this is told from a single point of view, which I found to be refreshing. <br/><br/>I really related to Erin, the protagonist, and felt comfortable sitting with her voice the whole way through. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1545762914ra/26808618.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>A documentary filmmaker, Erin is working on a long-term project interviewing convicted criminals on the eve of their release and just after. I</span>
  <span id="freeText2445707922297204372" style="display:none"><b>**3.5-stars**</b><br><br>A solid Summer read! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491417804ra/22408909.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Something in the Water</i> starts in a very peculiar place, quickly drawing me into the story.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1524417499ra/25416681.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In contrast to a lot of what I am reading lately, this is told from a single point of view, which I found to be refreshing. <br><br>I really related to Erin, the protagonist, and felt comfortable sitting with her voice the whole way through. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1545762914ra/26808618.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>A documentary filmmaker, Erin is working on a long-term project interviewing convicted criminals on the eve of their release and just after. In the midst of all of this, she marries the man of her dreams. <br><br>Mark, the dream guy, is a once successful investment banker who comes under great stress due to difficulties with his career. The biggest one being he doesn't have one anymore. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1555526855ra/27377254.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>With all of this going on the couple decide to go on a honeymoon to Bora Bora. <br><br>Whilst there, on a private scuba diving excursion, they discover something in the water that will forever change the course of their lives.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1555526855ra/27377255.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>This book has mystery, intrigue, intense moments and appalling moments. <br><br>Frankly, it's a lot; an excellent examination of what humans are willing to do for something valuable. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1555526855ra/27377256.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If you value wealth and stability, what would you do to get and maintain that? <br>What sorts of lines would you cross? <br>Would you be the same person? <br>Are you any different from any other person who may have crossed lines of their own? <br><br>I found the story formatted in such a way that it kept me guessing. It kept me wanting to keep turning pages and although I found a lot of the main characters decisions insane, who is to say I wouldn't do the same in her place? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1595342577ra/29850251.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I would definitely recommend this as a quick beach read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2445707922297204372" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
