<div id="review_2444350076" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2444350076" />
    <a title="Umut Rados" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24816039-umut-rados"><img alt="Umut Rados" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576844432p2/24816039.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2444350076?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Umut Rados" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Umut Rados" href="/user/show/24816039-umut-rados">Umut Rados</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2444350076&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2444350076" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14152498581036939453">For full rant review, please visit my blog: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://umutreviews.wordpress.com/2018/07/06/dont-do-this-to-yourselves-people-something-in-the-water/'>https://umutreviews.wordpress.com/201...</a><br/><br/>Warning: This review contains spoilers. There’s no other way of ranting without giving it away.<br/><br/>I must admit, the first pages were intriguing. The book opens with a woman digging a grave to bury her husband. Why wouldn’t it be intriguing! She gave a loooong narrative of how to dig a grave, obstacles, bla bla. But, I thought it was to pull the reader in by making it interesting at the beginning. I shouldn’t have fa</span>
  <span id="freeText14152498581036939453" style="display:none">For full rant review, please visit my blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://umutreviews.wordpress.com/2018/07/06/dont-do-this-to-yourselves-people-something-in-the-water/">https://umutreviews.wordpress.com/201...</a><br /><br />Warning: This review contains spoilers. There’s no other way of ranting without giving it away.<br /><br />I must admit, the first pages were intriguing. The book opens with a woman digging a grave to bury her husband. Why wouldn’t it be intriguing! She gave a loooong narrative of how to dig a grave, obstacles, bla bla. But, I thought it was to pull the reader in by making it interesting at the beginning. I shouldn’t have fallen into that trap!<br /><br />This looooong and unnecessary narratives continued with our couple choosing the wedding menu (yes, you read right, the wedding menu! with all the details of it! different options! all of it!). Further down, we go into their honeymoon travel, all the first class details, which doors to pass through, bla bla. Then, a description of a gun, for many, MANY pages. A pregnancy test, etc. Did you sleep yet? No? Let’s move on then.<br /><br />THE PLOT: We open with Erin, our protagonist, digging this grave for her husband. Then we flash back to the past to come to that point. They prepare for their wedding. Mark is an investment banker, Erin is a documentary producer. We are already 30% in before the big twist happens in the book, which is finding SOMETHING in the water. Mark loses his job. Erin proves a moron early on as she has no idea of their financial situation if Mark won’t work. Erin is also making a documentary with some prisoners, and we get to know them very well as well, ALL 3 of them. At this point, I’m innocently thinking these guys will connect to the story in a logical way.<br /><br />Then finally, at their honeymoon in Bora Bora, they find a plane wreck and a bag full of money and diamonds, a USB and a phone. Honestly, after this point, there are no words enough to tell how silly it gets. Erin makes many stupid mistakes like opening the phone. They smuggle the money and diamonds in the country like it’s a normal thing. All 2 million pounds! Dear UK Border Force, I would take it as an offence. Then of course the owners of these (The dangerous Russians) come on board. Erin asks help from Eddie (one of the prisoners) for help. (I don’t know even where that came from, since when they were friends). Also, Eddie helps with all the diamond selling, hiding the money, in return if Erin speaks to his daughter which he want to win over again. WTF!!! Eddie must be the most naive gangster of all times.<br /><br />Then all of a sudden, Mark decides to be the bad guy. He cooperates with Russians, tries to get all the money for himself. In the middle, we learn Erin is pregnant. Some Patrick guy appears out of the blue! Don’t ask people! It even hurts to write this.<br /><br />If you’re not even convinced with the plot, let’s move on to the UN-ATTENTION to DETAIL:<br /><br />Apparently Ashar Farooq is a Turkish name according to the book. Interesting. I’m Turkish and I never heard of that. Of course it’s an Arabic name, and he’s going to Syria. But, for Steadman, what’s the difference apparently. Turkish, Arab, all the same. Well, NOT AT ALL. I’d expect her to do some research on Google at least to differentiate ethnicities properly.<br />Again, apparently, Gaziantep is a small village in Turkey. It’s a city with 2 million population! It annoyed the hell out of me. Writing a book and not looking up even this!<br />These are the ones I could detect, I can’t imagine the ones I couldn’t and the writer feels entitled to give whatever information she wants.<br /><br />Still not convinced?? Let’s move on to the WRITING STYLE. Which style? Oh, wait, LACK of style!<br /><br />I don’t know even where to begin. It was a complete mish-mash of whatever. It was like somebody wrote the beginning, another the middle, then another finished the book. And all those f…ing details that don’t add ANYTHING to the plot. I could easily cut half of the book without losing anything of the plot.<br /><br />So, I really can’t get the 4-5 stars. It’s one of the worst books I read this year, and ever.<br /><br />Steadman had a small part in Downton Abbey, which is one of my favourite shows. I don’t think I will even watch where she appears again. YES, it was THAT BAD.<br /><br />1 star is even generous. I wouldn’t recommend this book to anyone. I’m very surprised with the buzz, and even that it’s published.<br /><br />Thanks to NetGalley and the publisher for granting a free copy in exchange for an honest review.<br /><br />And thanks to you if you reached till the end of my rant 🙂 Happy reading with better books!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14152498581036939453" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2476064528" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2476064528" />
    <a title="Norma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41400192-norma"><img alt="Norma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589038160p2/41400192.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2476064528?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Norma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Norma" href="/user/show/41400192-norma">Norma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41400192-norma?shelf=traveling-sister-reads">traveling-sister-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2476064528" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13695123516904467262">3.5 Stars rounded up because I definitely found this book to be entertaining and had me totally glued to those pages! <br/><br/>SOMETHING IN THE WATER by CATHERINE STEADMAN is an engaging, refreshing, and a steady paced thriller that immediately drew me in with its opening scene and had me totally intrigued in finding out what was in the water. <br/><br/>So here’s the thing about my experience with this book. I have never been so unsure about my feelings about a book after finishing as I was with this one. There we</span>
  <span id="freeText13695123516904467262" style="display:none">3.5 Stars rounded up because I definitely found this book to be entertaining and had me totally glued to those pages! <br /><br />SOMETHING IN THE WATER by CATHERINE STEADMAN is an engaging, refreshing, and a steady paced thriller that immediately drew me in with its opening scene and had me totally intrigued in finding out what was in the water. <br /><br />So here’s the thing about my experience with this book. I have never been so unsure about my feelings about a book after finishing as I was with this one. There were so many parts that I enjoyed and was totally entertained by, but then after finishing it, I was a little underwhelmed and disappointed by the whole story in general. I thought this story had so much potential to be a great one. Although, I will say that I thoroughly enjoyed CATHERINE STEADMAN’S descriptive writing style though which kept me totally invested in this story. Here is a quote from the book that I absolutely loved.<br /><br /> “But now that I can see her, I understand that those silences, which sounded empty over the phone, were actually very full. I just couldn’t see before what they were full of.”<br /> <br />CATHERINE STEADMAN delivers an insightful and well-written novel here that I would consider to be more of a slow-burner than a heart pounding and gripping thriller. The novel has an interesting enough premise with a touch of unease to the storyline and characters that well - I will let you experience for yourself. I will say though that I actually quite enjoyed the main character and didn’t experience some of the same issues that other readers did. I felt like she was true to herself and telling us a totally unedited version of her story and events. <br /><br />Overall, even though I had some reservations about this story, I still found it to be a compulsive read with a few good twists. I was very engaged and interested in how this story was going to all play out. Would recommend!<br /><br />* Traveling Friends Group Read <br /><br />Review written and posted on our themed book blog:<br />Two Sisters Lost In A Coulee Reading<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twosisterslostinacoulee.com">https://twosisterslostinacoulee.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13695123516904467262" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2326092544" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10729865469811280535"><b>4 shocking stars to Something in the Water!</b> 🏝 🏝 🏝 🏝 <br/><br/>Erin films documentaries, and her new husband, Mark, is an investment banker. They fly to the honeymoon of a lifetime to Bora Bora. Everything is tropical and picture-perfect, until they find <i>something in the water</i> while scuba diving. Dun dun dun. <br/><br/>Erin and Mark have to decide if they will tell the truth or keep a secret. Either way, danger potentially awaits...<br/><br/>This book starts out with a bombshell when Erin and Mark find something in the water.</span>
  <span id="freeText10729865469811280535" style="display:none"><b>4 shocking stars to Something in the Water!</b> 🏝 🏝 🏝 🏝 <br /><br />Erin films documentaries, and her new husband, Mark, is an investment banker. They fly to the honeymoon of a lifetime to Bora Bora. Everything is tropical and picture-perfect, until they find <i>something in the water</i> while scuba diving. Dun dun dun. <br /><br />Erin and Mark have to decide if they will tell the truth or keep a secret. Either way, danger potentially awaits...<br /><br />This book starts out with a bombshell when Erin and Mark find something in the water...The next chunk of the book is slower-building until you get towards the last third, where the tension builds and my heartrate soared!<br /><br />I loved Erin and Mark and was completely intrigued by their relationship and how they balanced each other out. They each struggle with what decision to make and how to make the decision together as a couple. <br /><br />The side characters who are prisoners Erin is filming in her documentary added a secondary story that I found enthralling. <br /><br />Something in the Water is both thrilling and engaging. The premise was fresh, and the writing was taut. Overall, I was left wondering what I would do if I had been in Mark and Erin’s shoes. <br /><br />Thank you to Caroline Steadman, Random House/Ballantine, and Netgalley for the ARC. Something in the Water will be released on June 5, 2018. <br /><br />My reviews can also be found on my blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jennifertarheelreader.com">www.jennifertarheelreader.com</a></span>

But then we go back and it reads more like chick lit. I found Erin initially very irritating. She had no clue about adjusting to her circumstances.   <span id="freeText13610126682258763362" style="display:none">3.5 Stars<br />This is billed as a thriller. But 1/3 in, I was still waiting. Yes, you know within the first few minutes that Erin is digging a grave. But then we go back and it reads more like chick lit. I found Erin initially very irritating. She had no clue about adjusting to her circumstances. She did grow on me and by the end of the book I liked her and appreciated her initiative. <br />This is a very slow burn leading up to the big discovery. And even after the discovery, the pace doesn’t really pick up until the very end. It’s just a pretty slow moving book. In fact, throughout the book, I kept thinking a better editing job would have gone a long way to making this book more exciting. That said, the ending is very good. <br />This is all about secrets, especially the secrets spouses keeps from each other. But it was just too apparent to me what was happening and how we ended up with that dead body. <br />Steadman does a very good job narrating her own book. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3346479951588318624">This is a thriller about a couple who find themselves in financial distress weeks before their wedding and the decisions they make afterwards will have life-changing consequences. <br/><br/>Erin is a documentary filmmaker and Mark is a banker who loses his job days before the big day. They live in a very nice home and decide to go through with their planned wedding as well as the honeymoon despite the fact that they could make wiser financial decisions under the circumstances.<br/> <br/>Once in their dreamy Bora-Bo</span>
  <span id="freeText3346479951588318624" style="display:none">This is a thriller about a couple who find themselves in financial distress weeks before their wedding and the decisions they make afterwards will have life-changing consequences. <br /><br />Erin is a documentary filmmaker and Mark is a banker who loses his job days before the big day. They live in a very nice home and decide to go through with their planned wedding as well as the honeymoon despite the fact that they could make wiser financial decisions under the circumstances.<br /> <br />Once in their dreamy Bora-Bora honeymoon, they find "something in the water" <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[that could resolve all their money troubles <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> but may also end up putting their lives in danger. <br /><br />The book opens up with an engaging scene where Erin is digging a grave to bury a body. Then the timeline moves back into the past and describes the events that led up to that moment.<br /><br />I liked the characters but at some points I was frustrated by their decisions. It is true that the factors such as motivation and opportunity were present for Erin and Mark to behave the way they did, but still. <br /><br />Overall, the novel was engaging and the author kept the plot moving forward. I recommend it to readers of thrillers and contemporary fiction. <br /><br /><i>I received an advance copy from the publisher via Netgalley </i></span>

<div id="review_2455768042" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2455768042" />
    <a title="Brandice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36348070-brandice"><img alt="Brandice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582594594p2/36348070.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2455768042?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brandice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brandice" href="/user/show/36348070-brandice">Brandice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2455768042" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8090879044538573492">I listened to <i>Something in the Water</i> via audiobook, read by the author, Catherine Steadman, and I really enjoyed it. I’m pretty sure I would have enjoyed the book regardless, but I found her narration and British accent to be soothing. Her characters and setting descriptions were vivid. The “thing” in the water was much different than what I anticipated prior to reading the book, which wasn’t a bad thing at all. <br/><br/>Erin Locke is making a documentary about prisoners and their upcoming releases. Her </span>
  <span id="freeText8090879044538573492" style="display:none">I listened to <i>Something in the Water</i> via audiobook, read by the author, Catherine Steadman, and I really enjoyed it. I’m pretty sure I would have enjoyed the book regardless, but I found her narration and British accent to be soothing. Her characters and setting descriptions were vivid. The “thing” in the water was much different than what I anticipated prior to reading the book, which wasn’t a bad thing at all. <br /><br />Erin Locke is making a documentary about prisoners and their upcoming releases. Her fiancé and eventual husband, Mark Roberts, is an investment banker. The story begins by setting the scene of their daily life in London and their wedding planning. There is tension surrounding them and the wedding, due to financial strain. The couple goes to Bora Bora for their honeymoon and while scuba diving, finds something in the water that changes their lives moving forward. The rest of the story follows their course of action as Erin and Mark decide what to do, and how to do it. <br /><br />As many reviewers have noted, it takes awhile for the story to get going - While I enjoyed the first part of the book, detailing the couple’s routine life and wedding preparation, it didn’t have a ton of connection to the heart of the story. Even after the scuba diving incident, I wouldn’t describe this as a fast-paced thriller. That said, I did really enjoy <i>Something in the Water</i>, finding myself curious to see what Erin and Mark’s next moves would be, as each move heightened the story and I remained interested in the outcome through the end of the book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8090879044538573492" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5835690487293675269">4.25 Stars → This anxiety-inducing book was A LOT of fun to read. It's gotten major buzz since it's a Reese's Book Club pick. There were 200 holds for it at my library, but I noticed ONE copy was available on the Limited Loan shelf at the branch across town. Of course, I’m there when they opened that morning to elbow my way to the top. I had to know what’s in the water!!<br/><br/>The opening chapter starts with a bang.   <span id="freeText5835690487293675269" style="display:none">4.25 Stars → This anxiety-inducing book was A LOT of fun to read. It's gotten major buzz since it's a Reese's Book Club pick. There were 200 holds for it at my library, but I noticed ONE copy was available on the Limited Loan shelf at the branch across town. Of course, I’m there when they opened that morning to elbow my way to the top. I had to know what’s in the water!!<br /><br />The opening chapter starts with a bang. You're left wondering, how in the heck did it come to that?? The set-up: A honeymooning couple make a shocking discovery on their trip to Bora Bora. OK, so after the stunning opening, the pacing was very slow until about the 30% mark. I think I was just TOO impatient - waiting, waiting, waiting - to find out what was in the water. And then, thunk thunk thunk...<br /><br />SOMETHING IN THE WATER was such an entertaining book, but also made me very nervous! Some of the decisions the characters made (especially Erin) made me STOP to blink my eyes repeatedly. What were you thinking??<br /><br />After the big discovery, the author did a fantastic job keeping the suspense going and the pages turning. I can't think of a more perfect "beach" thriller to read this summer. This is Catherine Steadman's debut novel (wow!), and I'm looking forward to reading more from her in the future.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2408678202" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer2948724768433596255">This is a refreshing take on the psychological thriller trope. The beginning is more than just a little intriguing. How long does it actually take to bury a body? From there the build and character development slow down significantly until it picks up about midway. Ethics come into question, criminal behavior is more exhausting than one might imagine and you may not know another as well as you think you do. Satisfying but not necessarily harrowing.</span>

Passionately in love, they embark on a dream honeymoon to the tropical island of Bora Bora, where they enjoy the sun, the sand, and each other. Then, while scuba diving in the crystal blue sea, they find something in the water. ...<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز هفتم ماه می سال 2019میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: چیزی درون آب؛ نویسنده: کاترین استدمن؛ مترجم: آرش خوش‌صفا؛ تهران انتشارات روزگار‏‫، 1397؛ در 410ص؛ شابک 9789643748821؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان بریتانیایی - سده 21م‬<br /><br />کتاب «چیزی درون آب»؛ نخستین رمان «کاترین استدمن» نامزد عنوان پرفروش‌ترین کتاب هیجان‌انگیز و اسرارآمیز سال 2018میلادی، از نظر کاربران گودریدز، و از پرفروش‌های این سال بود؛ «ارین» یک مستندساز، در آستانه ی موفقیت بزرگ کاری است، «مارک» هم کارمند خوش‌تیپ بانک است، که ایده‌ ها و نقشه‌ های بسیاری در سرش دارد؛ این زوج با عشقی فزاینده تصمیم می‌گیرند، برای ماه عسل، به جزیره ی استوایی «بورابورا» بروند، و می‌خواهند از آفتاب و ماسه و طبیعت آنجا، لذت ببرند؛ آنها یک روز، در حین غواصی در آب شفاف دریا، چیزهایی بسیار دردسرساز و خطرناک پیدا میکنند؛ حالا آنها مجبور هستند، تصمیم بگیرند؛ یا باید همه چیز را به پلیس گزارش کنند، و یا آن را مانند رازی، با خود نگاه دارند<br /><br />نقل از متن: «سوراخ رویش کاملاً پیداست؛ ولی خب انگار دیشب خیلی کار زیادی باهاش نکردیم؛ خدایا، واقعاً که وقتی آدم مست می‌کند، عقلش را از دست می‌دهد؛ متوجه دوتا چسب زخمی می‌شوم، که روی دست مارک است؛ پس حتماً دیشب خود او بوده، که با قیچیه کار کرده؛ می‌روم می‌نشینم روی تخت، و کیسه‌ هه را وارسی می‌کنم؛ سوراخی که رویش زدیم، به درد نمی‌خورد؛ حتی یک انگشت هم داخلش نمی‌رود، که بشود گشادترش کرد، و نمی‌شود هیچ از داخلش دید؛ به این می‌گویند ضربه محکم، و اثر ضعیف؛ سرم را می‌گیرم بالا، و نگاهی به «مارک» می‌اندازم؛ هنوزم می‌تونیم تحویلش بدیم؟ - آره، معلومه؛ می‌گیم وقتی پیداش کردیم همین ریختی بود؛ خب افتاده بوده توی دریا دیگه، ها؟ - انگار اصلاً نگران چیزی نیست؛ - اگه همچین سوراخی بشه روش زد، می‌شه یه سوراخ دیگه هم دوباره دُرُس کرد؟ زل می‌زنم به چشم‌هاش؛ شانه‌ ای بالا می‌اندازد، و قیچی را از روی میز پاتختی، پرت می‌کند سمت من؛ در حالیکه حواسش دوباره پرت «اَتِنبرو» می‌شود، به‌م می‌گوید: «خودت یه امتحانی بکن.»؛ پایان نقل<br /><br />استدمن در این رمان، یک داستان روان‌شناسانه و مجذوب‌ کننده می‌نگارد؛ داستانی که شاید دلتان بخواهد شما هم، لب ساحل آن را بخوانید؛ در هر صورت این داستان آدرنالین خونتان را بسیار بالا خواهد برد<br /><br />تاریخ بهنگام رسانی 19/06/1399هجری خورشیدی؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2317845412417055801"><b>What an intriguing read, just the book to wile away the hours by the pool on my holiday</b><br/><br/>Something in the water by Catherine Steadman grabbed my attention while I was reading a goodread's friends review and I knew this was going to be on my holiday read list. <br/><br/>The Novel opens with a woman digging a grave and her descriptions of same really feed the reader's imagination and you just want to find out the whys and when and how. This is the sort of book where you want to shout at the characters, where </span>
  <span id="freeText2317845412417055801" style="display:none"><b>What an intriguing read, just the book to wile away the hours by the pool on my holiday</b><br /><br />Something in the water by Catherine Steadman grabbed my attention while I was reading a goodread's friends review and I knew this was going to be on my holiday read list. <br /><br />The Novel opens with a woman digging a grave and her descriptions of same really feed the reader's imagination and you just want to find out the whys and when and how. This is the sort of book where you want to shout at the characters, where you find yourself wincing and talking out loud if reading in public places and where good a old fashioned thriller style plot with lots of twists and turns keeps you guessing right up to the end.<br /><br />I listened to this one on audible and high praise for the narrator Catherine Steadman, I do love when an author reads her own work as I find they know their book and their characters and with Something In The Water this works so well.<br />I enjoyed this easy read but will this one stay with me a year from now remains to be seen. </span>

<div id="review_2283198523" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Lucy Langford" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/74034800-lucy-langford"><img alt="Lucy Langford" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518091381p2/74034800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2283198523?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucy Langford" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucy Langford" href="/user/show/74034800-lucy-langford">Lucy Langford</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2283198523" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9411734908991385705">4****<br/><br/><i>Have you ever wondered how to dig a grave? Wonder no longer. It takes an age. However long you think it takes, double that.</i><br/><br/>This book had one of the best openings ever. After that, there is a slow build to the <i>something in the water </i> and the tumultuous set of events that happen after.<br/><br/>Erin, a documentary filmmaker with the chance of a career breakthrough; Mark, a handsome investment banker. The slow build to this book builds on Erin and Mark's picture perfect relationship, they seem to have i</span>
  <span id="freeText9411734908991385705" style="display:none">4****<br /><br /><i>Have you ever wondered how to dig a grave? Wonder no longer. It takes an age. However long you think it takes, double that.</i><br /><br />This book had one of the best openings ever. After that, there is a slow build to the <i>something in the water </i> and the tumultuous set of events that happen after.<br /><br />Erin, a documentary filmmaker with the chance of a career breakthrough; Mark, a handsome investment banker. The slow build to this book builds on Erin and Mark's picture perfect relationship, they seem to have it all. However, cracks appear when Mark loses his job. To balance this unfortunate situation the two try to make it work... booking their dream honeymoon.<br /><br />During their honeymoon to Bora Bora there is <i>Something in the Water</i> leading to an interesting set of events. After all... no one knows about their discovery- right?<br /><br />This is a story of deception, manipulation and lies and features fascinating characters along the way! <br /><br /><i>Mistakes come down to three things: (1) lack of time, (2) lack of initiative, (3) lack of care.</i><br /><br />While Erin's actions have been criticised (by myself included), Catherine Steadman does a brilliant job at delving into the logical and illogical psyche that most of us have, which can lead to making questionable decisions. It was great to see a very pro-action character in Erin albeit sometimes these actions seem "wrong", there was not much hand-wringing and Catherine Steadman shows a character being in control and making her own decisions.<br /><br />I thought the documentary film-making parts of Erin's work were completely fascinating. As a true crime documentary junkie, I loved learning how Erin directs her documentary to explore prison and after-prison life in a few selective people. Catherine Steadman creates these fantastic characters that Erin interviews, each of them prisoners with their own unique crimes, as well as their own individuality.<br /><br />One of the points that has been critiqued in this book is the form of bonds of "friendship" between Erin and some of the prisoners, more specifically the "friendship" between Erin and the character of Eddie Bishop (who is a big deal in the crime world) and how implausible/ stupid her decision is in asking him for advice. I actually really liked the way Erin interacted with these characters, especially Eddie Bishop, and how each interaction with each prisoner was so different to the other. <br /><br />The events in this book are not entirely implausible, unlikely maybe, but not too far removed from what could happen in real life. While you can become frustrated at some of the decisions made in this book, I think Steadman does a brilliant job at describing a characters internal thought process, the cycles of logical and illogical thought, with conflicting decisions, and recognises the individuality in the decision-making process.<br /><br />I highly enjoyed this read. It was extremely addictive and compelling and my heart and mind were racing to get to the end... I kept having to re-read parts as I was so desperate to read how the scenes unfolded.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9411734908991385705" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2326551397" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2326551397" />
    <a title="Carrie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36817401-carrie"><img alt="Carrie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415677371p2/36817401.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2326551397?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carrie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carrie" href="/user/show/36817401-carrie">Carrie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/36488805-something-in-the-water">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36817401-carrie?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2326551397" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12485658090744894139">Something In The Water by Catherine Steadman is a thriller that certainly had an opening that should grab readers right away, the main character digging a grave. After finding out that there would be a need for a grave readers jump back in time to find out just what led to that event.<br/><br/>Erin and Mark seem to be very much in love and excited to be planning their wedding and honeymoon. Erin is a budding filmmaker working on a documentary in which she’s interviewing criminals and Mark a successful inv</span>
  <span id="freeText12485658090744894139" style="display:none">Something In The Water by Catherine Steadman is a thriller that certainly had an opening that should grab readers right away, the main character digging a grave. After finding out that there would be a need for a grave readers jump back in time to find out just what led to that event.<br /><br />Erin and Mark seem to be very much in love and excited to be planning their wedding and honeymoon. Erin is a budding filmmaker working on a documentary in which she’s interviewing criminals and Mark a successful investment banker. However when Mark loses his job that is where things start to get a little shaky in their perfect bubble.<br /><br />With the honeymoon already set to happen Erin and Mark agree to set their troubles aside and still go on the vacation to Bora Bora. Sun and surf and adventure seems to be just what the couple need to bring them right back together. When out scuba diving though they make a find in the water that will lead them down a very dangerous path.<br /><br />Something In The Water was actually very engaging and kept the pages turning rather easily as the events unfolded. For me though as much as I liked finding out more and more I also struggled some with liking Erin, she would get a bit frantic which I would sometimes find annoying. If it really weren’t for those moments though I would have rated higher than 3.5 stars since the story was one that was rather fun to watch unfold and with this being a debut novel I would certainly be interested in reading more in the future.<br /><br />I received an advance copy from the publisher via NetGalley.<br /><br />For more review please visit <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://carriesbookreviews.com/">https://carriesbookreviews.com/</a> </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2407205844" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2407205844" />
    <a title="Carol" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7668522-carol"><img alt="Carol" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546364878p2/7668522.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2407205844?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol" href="/user/show/7668522-carol">Carol</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7668522-carol?shelf=debut">debut</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7668522-carol?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2407205844" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9558817274192962050"><b>3.5 Stars with a roundup to 4.0 because I REALLY could NOT put it down!</b><p><b> "Digging a grave is very hard"</b> as you will discover after reading the first chapter entitled, of course, The Grave.</p><p> It all begins with an actual grave being dug, then quickly reverts back in time to the start of a new relationship, marriage and big plans for the future. Then, even though a big disappointment for the newlyweds rears itself, the expensive first class South Pacific honeymoon goes on....and an eerie and intense </p></span>
  <span id="freeText9558817274192962050" style="display:none"><b>3.5 Stars with a roundup to 4.0 because I REALLY could NOT put it down!</b><p><b> "Digging a grave is very hard"</b> as you will discover after reading the first chapter entitled, of course, The Grave.</p><p> It all begins with an actual grave being dug, then quickly reverts back in time to the start of a new relationship, marriage and big plans for the future. Then, even though a big disappointment for the newlyweds rears itself, the expensive first class South Pacific honeymoon goes on....and an eerie and intense atmosphere ensues. It's this feeling of the <b>Not Knowing</b> what or who to trust that kept me glued to the pages.</p><p> That <b>SOMETHING <u>IN</u> THE WATER</b> was not at all what I thought it would be....but better!</p><p> Super entertaining....and one fine debut for Catherine Steadman! And, ok, one downside <i>(for me)</i>.....one of the main characters is naive, reckless and, YES, just plain stupid at times, but <b>STILL.....</b>great summer read!</p></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('B36v2jt9DLxBZWpUFg8CNS1Eq1wFohZI0F7KiX+yDuJp2a4qP5e2vX8AQCet457l8XEmjB76XA0ljlnAbVhY4Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wwSeU5wNgrOqe1or1uN22K28rO33jWhu592k9GqlfjSto5+jmOc4spQecFhtD+oIcYkhPezVIisSDTe9eE8oNw==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/16847770.Catherine_Steadman">About Catherine Steadman</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/16847770.Catherine_Steadman"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1507661828p3/16847770.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/16847770.Catherine_Steadman">Catherine Steadman
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
1,822
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4329992050732097543">Catherine Steadman is an actress and writer based in North London, UK. She is best known for her role as Mabel Lane Fox in Downton Abbey and is currently filming on the new Starz television series 'The Rook'. She grew up in the New Forest, UK, and lives with a small dog and an average sized man. Something in the Water is her first novel.<br/><br/>(source: Amazon)</span>

</div>
</div>
